## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ODE for concentration change over time, characteristic of chemical kinetics. With only A and t available, the most likely structures are single-species rate laws (decay/production), possibly with time-varying rate coefficients or empirical deactivation terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production over time)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, many dilute-limit reactions)
- Second-order (single-species) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with same reactant or dimerization-limited forms)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical order, c1 not necessarily integer)
- Linear source–sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant generation with first-order removal; approach to steady state)
- Autocatalytic / quadratic growth then limitation (single-species): dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-amplification with depletion/limiting term in terms of A alone)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (exponential approach of A to equilibrium level c1)
- Time-dependent first-order rate (activation/deactivation): dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * t) (rate coefficient drifting approximately linearly in time)
- Exponentially time-varying rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (accelerating or slowing kinetics due to changing conditions)
- Power-law time dependence (aging/catalyst decay effect): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (t + c1)**c2 (effective rate changes with elapsed time)
- Mixed-order with baseline loss: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * A) * A (first + second order combined without introducing extra species)
- Rational (self-inhibition / saturation in the rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate per A decreases at high A due to crowding/inhibition expressed only via A)
- Rational with accelerating loss at high A: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (interpolates between first- and second-order regimes)
- Empirical polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (local approximation to kinetics near an operating range)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If A is being consumed in a closed system, dA_dt should be non-positive for A > 0; candidate forms often include an overall negative sign times a nonnegative function of A.
- Reaction rates typically vanish as A -> 0 for pure consumption (no source term), suggesting factors like A or A**n multiplying the rate coefficient.
- Order identification: log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) approximately linear implies power-law order; curvature suggests mixed-order or rational forms.
- Equilibrium/steady-state behavior: dA_dt = 0 at A = A_eq indicates structures like -(A - c1) or c0 - c1*A; multiple zeros can indicate polynomial kinetics.
- Time-varying environment (temperature, catalyst activity) can be absorbed into k(t); look for separable forms dA_dt = -A * k(t) with k(t) modeled as (c0+c1*t), exp(c*t), or (t+c1)^c2.
- Half-life dependence distinguishes orders: constant half-life suggests first-order; half-life increasing with initial A suggests second-order; decreasing suggests zero-order (until depletion).
- Positivity preservation: physically A(t) should remain >= 0; models with strong negative source terms (e.g., -c0 without safeguards) can drive A negative unless constrained to time windows before depletion.
- Stiffness/fast initial transients: large effective k or high-order A**n can create rapid early change followed by slow tails; rational forms can mimic regime switches without explicit piecewise terms.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK10)

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_t*sin(log(A + c3))
Candidates evaluated: 130
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to find candidates that are mathematically equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.17496*A² + 0.59132*sin(log(A + 1))`

This is a function of A only (t is absorbed into the constant c2*_t = 0.17496*3.37985 ≈ 0.59132). The GT has two basis functions: **A²** and **sin(log(A+1))**.

Let me note that `sin(log(A+1))` can be written using the identity:
`sin(θ) = cos(θ - π/2)`, so `sin(log(A+1)) = cos(log(A+1) - π/2)`

Also, since A ≥ 0, `|A| = A`, so `cos(c*log(c*|A|+1))` with appropriate constants could match `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me check candidates with the structure `c*A² + c*cos(c*log(c*|A|+1))` or `c*A² + c*sin(log(A+c))`:

**Candidate 22:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*|A|+1))`
Set c0=0, c1=2, c2=-0.17496. Then: `-0.17496*A² + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*A+1))`.
We need `c3*cos(c4*log(c5*A+1)) = 0.59132*sin(log(A+1))`.
Using `sin(x) = cos(x - π/2)`: set c5=1, c4=1, then `c3*cos(log(A+1)) ≠ sin(log(A+1))` unless we use a phase shift. But `cos(c4*log(...))` doesn't allow adding a phase shift inside. We'd need `cos(log(A+1) - π/2)` but the candidate only has `cos(c4*log(c5*|A|+1))`. There's no additive constant inside the cosine. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 119:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*cos(c4*log(c5*|A|+1)) + c6`
Same issue - no phase shift inside cosine. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 120:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2*cos(c3*log(c4*|A|+1)) + c5`
Same issue. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 45:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6*cos(c7*log(c8*|A|+1))`
Has sin(A*c4+c5) and cos(log), but sin(linear in A) ≠ sin(log(A+1)). Setting c3=0 leaves only cos without phase shift. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 74:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*|A|+1) + c6)`
Set c0=0, c1=0 (or c2→-∞ to kill exp). Then `c3*sin(c4*log(c5*A+1) + c6)`. With c4=1, c5=1, c6=0: `c3*sin(log(A+1))`. Plus we need A² term. But A*c1*exp(A*c2): set c2=0, then A*c1*exp(0)=A*c1. We need A², not A. Can't get A² from this. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 125:** `A*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3 + c4*cos(c5*log(c6*|A|+1)) + c7`
Set c2=2, c3=-0.17496, c0=c1=0, c7=0. Need `c4*cos(c5*log(c6*A+1)) = 0.59132*sin(log(A+1))`. No phase shift available. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 127:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3 + c4*cos(c5*log(c6*|A|+1))`
Same issue. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 63:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*exp(A*c4)*log(c5*t+1) + c6*sin(c7*log(c8*|A|+1) + c9)`
Set c0=0, c1=0, c3=0. Then `c6*sin(c7*log(c8*A+1)+c9)`. With c7=1, c8=1, c9=0: `c6*sin(log(A+1))`. But no A² term available (only A*linear or exp terms). **NO MATCH.**

After exhaustive analysis, none of the candidates can produce exactly `-0.17496*A² + 0.59132*sin(log(A+1))`.
